  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11593629237459851778">Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a thrilled audience of Addie, their govern</span>
  <span id="freeText11593629237459851778" style="display:none">Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a thrilled audience of Addie, their governess, and the young sorcerer Rhys. <br /><br />But when Meryl falls ill with the dreaded Gray Death, Addie must gather her courage and set off alone on a quest to find the cure and save her beloved sister. Addie takes the seven-league boots and magic spyglass left to her by her mother and the enchanted tablecloth and cloak given to her by Rhys - along with a shy declaration of his love. She prevails in encounters with tricky specters (spiders too) and outwits a wickedly personable dragon in adventures touched with romance and a bittersweet ending.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539026676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9341698824164080922"><br/>Follow Princess Addie as she is overcoming her fears in order to find a cure for her sister who had the mischance to fall into the claws of the Gray Death. This is a charming adventure brimming with princesses, dragons, elves, fairies, ogres, sorcerers and magic! Over and above that, it explores the themes of sisterly love and courage. Even a coward can be transformed into a knight. It can absolutely make a beautiful storytelling for children.</span>

        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=05-stars">05-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=physical-shelf">physical-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1843089231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12280443179776811243"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512940754ra/24648737.gif' alt='' width='350' height='196' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Starting off the new year correctly with a book about two sisters. One sister is a courageous blonde ready to find the cure to Sir Grey Death and the other is a brunette who is a coward who has to find her strength.<br/><br/>Meryl is the older sister. She dreams of fighting the dragons and rescuing her people from all the foes, including those small enough like Sir Grey Death.<br/><br/>The Grey Death is a long, drawn out processes that eventually kills its victim. With the cure prophesied, there is hope that someti</span>
  <span id="freeText12280443179776811243" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512940754ra/24648737.gif" alt="" width="350" height="196" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Starting off the new year correctly with a book about two sisters. One sister is a courageous blonde ready to find the cure to Sir Grey Death and the other is a brunette who is a coward who has to find her strength.<br><br>Meryl is the older sister. She dreams of fighting the dragons and rescuing her people from all the foes, including those small enough like Sir Grey Death.<br><br>The Grey Death is a long, drawn out processes that eventually kills its victim. With the cure prophesied, there is hope that sometime, someday soon, someone will find it.<br><br>Addie is a coward. She is terrified of spiders and she is terrified of losing her sister to her adventures. But when her sister comes down with the horrid Grey Death, she must find it in herself to go out and find the cure (since her good-for-nothing father The King won't).<br><br>I love this story more than anything. Gail Carson Levine made me cry through out the years reading this because I always pictured myself as Addie (the younger sister) and my sister Michelle as Meryl (the older sister). It breaks your heart, but not necessarily in a bad way.<br><br>Gail Carson Levine is known for her retellings of fairytales. This is an original of hers and it is absolutely something you should read very soon. It's a quick read, barely over 200 pages, but it is something that will make your heart warm and your face wet.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512940754ra/24648738.gif" alt="" width="350" height="192" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

          </span>

Even though Ella Enchanted is Gail Carson Levine's most well-known book, I think that The Two Princesses of Bamarre is her best book. It's really exciting, but also well-written. If you love Ella Enchanted, this is the book for you. </span>

<div id="review_447318189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/447318189" />
    <a title="Naomi Brist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12678407-naomi-brist"><img alt="Naomi Brist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347211693p2/12678407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/447318189?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi Brist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi Brist" href="/user/show/12678407-naomi-brist">Naomi Brist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12678407-naomi-brist?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer447318189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12609838725928055729">I've grown up with this story. To say that it has had an impact on my life is an incredible and unforgivable understatement. Everyone knows this author because of Ella Enchanted, but I believe that this book is much, much greater. It has romance, monsters, action, magic, and adventure; all things that people look for and enjoy in a good book. But what really makes this story great is not any of those things. What makes it great is how a young woman who is afraid of everything ventures out into a</span>
  <span id="freeText12609838725928055729" style="display:none">I've grown up with this story. To say that it has had an impact on my life is an incredible and unforgivable understatement. Everyone knows this author because of Ella Enchanted, but I believe that this book is much, much greater. It has romance, monsters, action, magic, and adventure; all things that people look for and enjoy in a good book. But what really makes this story great is not any of those things. What makes it great is how a young woman who is afraid of everything ventures out into a dangerous and terrifying world that would scare even the brave in order to save her sister even though there is a very high chance she might die in the attempt. Speaking as someone who has a lot of experience being afraid, this story is inspiring and very relatable in so many important areas. Because even those of us who are afraid of a great many things would go to frightening lengths and do the impossible to save someone we love. <br /><br />Two Princesses of Bamarre is a fantastic fairy tale that contains all the best elements of such stories and has more heart than stories written by authors that are supposed to be 'good'. If the apocalypse came tomorrow and there was only one book that I could keep with me and read again it would be this one. I love many books, but this is a part of my soul and is beyond beautiful. If you like fantasy and are not opposed to actual emotion (if you are then you are next on my hit list) then you should read this book. It is the fairy tale that surpasses all fairy tales and puts the Grimm brothers to shame. Thank you, Gail Carson Levine, for writing such an amazing story. You're one of the greatest reasons I myself plan on becoming a writer. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12609838725928055729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41359574?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HeavyReader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HeavyReader" href="/user/show/142816-heavyreader">HeavyReader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">girls who are into those wimpy Disney princesses and anyone who wants to read a good adventure</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/142816-heavyreader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41359574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14317314282434856792">This book is so good!<br/><br/>It did take me a while to get into it. The first half or so of the book is kind of slow going. Two sisters. One is bold. One is shy. Yawn.<br/><br/>But then in the middle, when the shy sister has to leave the castle to save her beloved sister's life, it gets REALLY exciting. Specters. Gryphons. Dragons. Battles. WOW! I could hardly put it down at that point.<br/><br/>There's also a story within a story, a legend of the kingdom, and it is as well done as the main story.<br/><br/>The almost end had me bawl</span>
  <span id="freeText14317314282434856792" style="display:none">This book is so good!<br /><br />It did take me a while to get into it. The first half or so of the book is kind of slow going. Two sisters. One is bold. One is shy. Yawn.<br /><br />But then in the middle, when the shy sister has to leave the castle to save her beloved sister's life, it gets REALLY exciting. Specters. Gryphons. Dragons. Battles. WOW! I could hardly put it down at that point.<br /><br />There's also a story within a story, a legend of the kingdom, and it is as well done as the main story.<br /><br />The almost end had me bawling, thinking about my own sister and how terrible it would be to lose her.<br /><br />I don't typically get into stories about princesses. As Boots of the Coup says, "Tell your teacher I said princess <i>are</i> evil/How they got all their money was to kill people." But I can stomach the feisty, smart, brave princesses in the books of Gail Carson Levine. She spins the whole traditional princess genre and makes these gals rock!<br /><br />Unlike other books by Gail Carson Levine, this one is not based on a traditional fairy tale (or at least not one that I know), but it's better than any of those "someday my prince will come" bullshit stories that I grew up with.<br /><br />Give this one to the girl in your life who's all into those wimpy Disney princesses.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14317314282434856792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1315913456347173951">This book is one of the first fantasy novels I ever read.   <span id="freeText1315913456347173951" style="display:none">This book is one of the first fantasy novels I ever read. It's one I loved from beginning to end, and it's one that I never tire of reading over and over again. It's the only book I've read more times than I can count on my one hand and several more on the other. This is an awesome read with great morals about finding courage in a world that is against you doing so. It's about family and the beauty of being there for each other, even if you're not quiet the same. It's got poetry, dragons, action, suspense, all the good stuff...and it's in one read. So enjoy if anyone thinks to read it! :D</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615383554" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615383554?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sydney Cornwall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sydney Cornwall" href="/user/show/19752859-sydney-cornwall">Sydney Cornwall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19752859-sydney-cornwall?shelf=eng-356">eng-356</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer615383554&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615383554" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17248956983398587121">Plot Summary:<br/><br/>The plot revolves around two sisters, Meryl and Addie. They are the princesses of Bamarre, a fantastical kingdom where sorcerers, fairies, and dragons are commonly known to be in existence. Addie is the shy, timid younger sister stereotype; she spends her free time doing embroidery. Meryl, on the other hand, loves adventure and swords and fighting. Addie makes Meryl promise her that she won't go off to kill any dragons or anything until Addie gets married--but everything gets thrown</span>
  <span id="freeText17248956983398587121" style="display:none">Plot Summary:<br /><br />The plot revolves around two sisters, Meryl and Addie. They are the princesses of Bamarre, a fantastical kingdom where sorcerers, fairies, and dragons are commonly known to be in existence. Addie is the shy, timid younger sister stereotype; she spends her free time doing embroidery. Meryl, on the other hand, loves adventure and swords and fighting. Addie makes Meryl promise her that she won't go off to kill any dragons or anything until Addie gets married--but everything gets thrown into a frenzy when Meryl catches the Grey Death. Addie has to step up and try to find the cure when her father turns into a pansy and doesn't try very hard. She encounters griffons, specters, and dragons; she has to learn to be confident and believe in herself. In the end, she does find the cure to the Grey Death. She's too late to save her sister; however, and Meryl encounters the transformation into a fairy, a very sacred being. Addie kind of brings the kingdom out of the terror from dark creatures and the Grey Death, a curse brought upon by a dragon of late, becomes diminished.<br /><br />My Opinion:<br />I rated this book a two. I didn't really enjoy reading it. I have to say, for a younger reader, it's a good choice--there are great lessons to be learned; also (though it's done very blatantly) the protagonist shows a lot of character development throughout the course of the book. There's a nice unpredictable twist at the end--I very much expected Meryl to be saved from the Grey Death and was surprised with the ingenuity of the final result. I think it's a good story, but I'm just very cynical and felt like it was too simply and immaturely written for me, but that's just me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17248956983398587121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Gabs {My Full Bookshelf Reviews}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabs {My Full Bookshelf Reviews}" href="/user/show/13635411-gabs-my-full-bookshelf-reviews">Gabs {My Full Bookshelf Reviews}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13635411-gabs-my-full-bookshelf-reviews?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13635411-gabs-my-full-bookshelf-reviews?shelf=possible-automatic-buy-authors">possible-automatic-buy-authors</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645771513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8457276058190110623">I didn't think that Gail Carson Levine could write anything more spectacular than Ella Enchanted. I'm not going to say that The Two Princesses of Bamarre was better than Ella Enchanted, but it definitely was as good as it. <br/><br/>Addie and Meryl had such a great relationship. I loved reading about them, and how Addie was willing to risk her life to save her sister from the Gray Death. <br/><br/>Rhys...sigh. Oh, Rhys. He's a very attractive sorceror, and I loved him! Gail Carson Levine created a romance that wasn</span>
  <span id="freeText8457276058190110623" style="display:none">I didn't think that Gail Carson Levine could write anything more spectacular than Ella Enchanted. I'm not going to say that The Two Princesses of Bamarre was better than Ella Enchanted, but it definitely was as good as it. <br /><br />Addie and Meryl had such a great relationship. I loved reading about them, and how Addie was willing to risk her life to save her sister from the Gray Death. <br /><br />Rhys...sigh. Oh, Rhys. He's a very attractive sorceror, and I loved him! Gail Carson Levine created a romance that wasn't cheesy or over the top romantic, but was very sweet and great to read.<br /><br />It was refreshing to read a fairy tale that hadn't been written before, because I had no idea how it would end! I was very impressed with the ending, as well. It was unexpected, but satisfying.<br /><br />The monsters in here are also pretty fun to learn about. THe specters, the gryphons, the ogres, and the dragons were all portrayed in a new way, and some I hadn't even read of before! <br /><br />All together, I gave this five stars because it is an amazing, original tale that kept my interest. It has a good chance of becoming one of my all-time favorites!</span>

<div id="review_44097181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44097181" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1947586-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363746570p2/1947586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44097181?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1947586-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060293154" href="/book/show/820241.The_Two_Princesses_of_Bamarre">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1947586-megan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44097181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14158823816655821916">This book was really cute! It's written in the first person, which was a change, as few of the books I read are, and the protagonist of the story is Princess Addie, a sweet but cowardly girl who couldn't be more different than her sister, Meryl. Princess Meryl is courageous and longs for adventures where she can kill dragons, gryphons, and ogres. Addie would rather stay safe at home and wishes for peace, not wars like her sister. The two are even opposites in appearance. Addie has dark brown hai</span>
  <span id="freeText14158823816655821916" style="display:none">This book was really cute! It's written in the first person, which was a change, as few of the books I read are, and the protagonist of the story is Princess Addie, a sweet but cowardly girl who couldn't be more different than her sister, Meryl. Princess Meryl is courageous and longs for adventures where she can kill dragons, gryphons, and ogres. Addie would rather stay safe at home and wishes for peace, not wars like her sister. The two are even opposites in appearance. Addie has dark brown hair and is tall while Meryl has blonde hair and is short.<br /><br />Still they are very close, and when Meryl contracts the Gray Death, of which there is no cure, Addie decides to overcome her fears and sets out to find a cure. Along the way she finds help from her father's sorcerer, Rhys, with whom she falls in love. The background of sorcerers in this story was very interesting. They're born when lightning strikes marble, and therefore have no family, and instead of a heartbeat, they have a life flame burning in their chests. Sorcerers can be male or female, but all have dark wavy hair and white eyelashes. Their magic usually consists of manipulating clouds into different shapes for different purposes, and perhaps the most amazing thing of all is that they can fly.<br /><br />On Addie's adventure, she comes up against ogres, gryphons, and a dragon, all while trying to find a cure for her sister, who doesn't have much time left. The ending was surprising and not what I expected exactly, but I really enjoyed this book. It's geared towards young adults and was only a little over 200 pages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14158823816655821916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_703117462" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/703117462" />
    <a title="Audrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23291482-audrey"><img alt="Audrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377189271p2/23291482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/703117462?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audrey" href="/user/show/23291482-audrey">Audrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23291482-audrey?shelf=favortie-books">favortie-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer703117462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2361981761848367747"> At first, I thought that since this book was going to be too princess-y, and medieval time-ish, I asked myself, "Why bother?" <br/><br/><br/> My conscious had told me, "Suck it up and read it fool. You'll like it. You always like princesses, now."<br/><br/><br/> And I did. Like it, I mean. This wonderful, original story has been on of my favorites. I loved it! I don't remember much, but I do remember about the princess thinking she was frail, weak, not strong at all like the older one, going on a bunch of journeys. She had </span>
  <span id="freeText2361981761848367747" style="display:none"> At first, I thought that since this book was going to be too princess-y, and medieval time-ish, I asked myself, "Why bother?" <br /><br /><br /> My conscious had told me, "Suck it up and read it fool. You'll like it. You always like princesses, now."<br /><br /><br /> And I did. Like it, I mean. This wonderful, original story has been on of my favorites. I loved it! I don't remember much, but I do remember about the princess thinking she was frail, weak, not strong at all like the older one, going on a bunch of journeys. She had some kind of cloth, I think, and with it, she had to say a few words, and then "_Voila!_" it contained so much food, and it was actually GOOD. That was like my day today, actually. I had a birthday party, (yes, I still love the parties. Nice get together with friends actually, so you don't lose touch, you know?) With brownies, cake, chips, pretzels, and the amazing popcorn. :) It all made me smile.<br /><br /><br /> So, anyways, I also remember this adventurous part with the dragon, and it had held her imprisoned in her cave. I forget how she found a way out. I honestly need to check this book out of the library again. It was a magnificent story, one that I will truly never forget. I suggest this book for everyone, from the elderly, to eight year olds. Are there eight year olds on here? That would be weird. But we can live with it. It doesn't matter, ya know? Although it would be weird. So yeah, if you have not read this book, read it!<br /><br /><br />Audrey</span>

I love her books, Ella Enchanted and Ever. They are great. However, I can’t say that this is my favorite ou</span>
  <span id="freeText17290353294412070971" style="display:none">In one of my very early post, I listed some of my favorite books. This book was, and still is, on that list! From the first time I read this to the most current, I still am intrigued every time I turn the first page. I mean, monsters, diseases, poems, heroes, dangers, desperation, romance—those few words definitely mean it has to be a good book.<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine is just an amazing author. I love her books, Ella Enchanted and Ever. They are great. However, I can’t say that this is my favorite out of the three that are mentioned in this blog post. I don’t have a favorite. All of them are absolutely awesome. I really like it that they can be read as young kids or as teenagers. Sure, they may be meant for “tweens,” but they are still awesome or teens.<br /><br />Just from the cover, I could tell the personalities of the two girls. One is “bold and brave,” while the other is “fearful and shy.” 5 stars to the cover designer and artist.<br /><br />Even though I haven’t read all of Gail Carson Levine’s books, I know that she is a super good author. I would recommend her as an author. And, I would definitely recommend this book. 5 stars to The Two Princesses of Bamarre. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/387440-jessica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6468421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12110748725017672985">Cute and funny (like all of Gail Carson Levine's books! :D)!!<br/><br/>Gail Carson Levine here creates a fairy tale of her own and gives it a characteristic grrrl-power twist. Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a</span>
  <span id="freeText12110748725017672985" style="display:none">Cute and funny (like all of Gail Carson Levine's books! :D)!!<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine here creates a fairy tale of her own and gives it a characteristic grrrl-power twist. Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a thrilled audience of Addie, their governess, and the young sorcerer Rhys. But when Meryl falls ill with the dreaded Gray Death, Addie must gather her courage and set off alone on a quest to find the cure and save her beloved sister. Addie takes the seven-league boots and magic spyglass left to her by her mother and the enchanted tablecloth and cloak given to her by Rhys--along with a shy declaration of his love. She prevails in encounters with tricky specters (spiders too) and outwits a wickedly personable dragon in adventures touched with romance and a bittersweet ending. Young fans of princess stories will gobble this one up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12110748725017672985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_997252137" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Molly Murphy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33062657-molly-murphy"><img alt="Molly Murphy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411847150p2/33062657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/997252137?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly Murphy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly Murphy" href="/user/show/33062657-molly-murphy">Molly Murphy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33062657-molly-murphy?shelf=action-adventure-the-occasional-pir">action-adventure-the-occasional-pir</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer997252137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13188073305958144705">Ok, the whole book, the whole great book, was RUINED by the horrible ending. <br/>First of all, I like that Meryl, the daring, adventurous, passionate one, was small. I love it when the small people are like that. Also, I love that Meryl was the oldest 'cause a lot of people protray the oldest as some wimpy, over-mature person who never gets into any adventures. Finally, the firstborn is the spitfire! <br/>And then I liked the twists, that Addie had to go and conquer all of her fears and learn to be stron</span>
  <span id="freeText13188073305958144705" style="display:none">Ok, the whole book, the whole great book, was RUINED by the horrible ending. <br />First of all, I like that Meryl, the daring, adventurous, passionate one, was small. I love it when the small people are like that. Also, I love that Meryl was the oldest 'cause a lot of people protray the oldest as some wimpy, over-mature person who never gets into any adventures. Finally, the firstborn is the spitfire! <br />And then I liked the twists, that Addie had to go and conquer all of her fears and learn to be strong and courageous. <br />But then, instead of being cured to fight battles and save her kingdom, fiery Meryl becomes a fairy- a FAIRY, people. But worst of all, she CALMS DOWN. No longer is she the fiesty warrior princess I grew to love, but some gentle, mild-mannered FAIRY. Ugh! <br />(P.S. This shelf is actually supposed to be called action-adventure-the-occasional-pirate, but the stupid computer kind of forgot the "ate" part at the end of "pirate". Just in case you were wondering. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6110011196503547759">I have a love/hate relationship with this book. I first read this book over a decade ago, and it took me on the same extreme emotional roller-coaster ride this time around as it did then. I swear, this book has made me cry bitter tears, given me bounds of hope, chilled my spine, and made me blush. I completely adore the setting and the creatures. The characters melt my heart and plot steals my breath every time. I can completely immerse myself in this world and those who inhabit it. Those of you</span>
  <span id="freeText6110011196503547759" style="display:none">I have a love/hate relationship with this book. I first read this book over a decade ago, and it took me on the same extreme emotional roller-coaster ride this time around as it did then. I swear, this book has made me cry bitter tears, given me bounds of hope, chilled my spine, and made me blush. I completely adore the setting and the creatures. The characters melt my heart and plot steals my breath every time. I can completely immerse myself in this world and those who inhabit it. Those of you who know me know how much I admire Mrs. Levine and enjoy her work. This is no exception. In fact, this is tied with Ella Enchanted for my favorite of her books! (It's like Pride and Prejudice and Sense and Sensibility: each one is always my favorite when it's the one in front of me!) I cannot recommend this book highly enough!!<br /><br />Re-read: 8/27/17</span>

  <span id="freeText7325942501277241713" style="display:none">Someone wise once said, “Fear is a reaction, courage is a decision.” Today, I applaud just how true this statement is. <br /><br />This book should be read by everyone, especially the young ones. <script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9LIBTUIrDFhv1ujfhp9hbmTGl/b9//JJ2mmQJjhEEenOlGif+XXFMMj9XL5xamuxsplwPjNyfC6BF9aX9Qfjcw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XZxhcd9xZ/jyc98TMSlDBGWEVa6Vj5REUTSsNlcoMOZnugijZC+ukFVYa3LG3Enbs9uyZlsCGiMKSuqHmmvCfA==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer10892998304001813818">Just letting you all know: I'm only going to review books I love. There's enough negative criticism without me piling on. A book is too hard to write.<br/><br/>Gail Carson Levine grew up in New York City and began writing seriously in 1987. Her first book for children, Ella Enchanted, was a 1998 Newbery Honor Book. Levine's other books include Fairest; Dave at Night, an ALA Notable Book and Best Book for Yo</span>
  <span id="freeText10892998304001813818" style="display:none">Just letting you all know: I'm only going to review books I love. There's enough negative criticism without me piling on. A book is too hard to write.<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine grew up in New York City and began writing seriously in 1987. Her first book for children, Ella Enchanted, was a 1998 Newbery Honor Book. Levine's other books include Fairest; Dave at Night, an ALA Notable Book and Best Book for Young Adults; The Wish; The Two Princesses of Bamarre; and the six Princess Tales books. She is also the author of the nonfiction book Writing Magic: Creating Stories That Fly and the picture book Betsy Who Cried Wolf, illustrated by Scott Nash. Gail, her husband, David, and their Airedale, Baxter, live in a 1790 farmhouse in the Hudson River Valley of New York State.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10892998304001813818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
